     return Err(WorkflowError::Backend(e));\n    93→            }\n    94→        };\n    95→\n    96→        let planning_response = match parse_planning_response(&response.output) {\n    97→            Ok(r) => r,\n    98→            Err(e) => {\n    99→                self.state = WorkflowState::Failed {\n   100→                    error: e.to_string(),\n   101→                };\n   102→ {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Y8v8JMWSBYbGMAHitMCvBw","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Planning Step — Feature Document\n     2→\n     3→**Product Area**: Coder\n     4→**Status**: Draft\n     5→**Updated**: 2026-03-06 (model listing/selection)\n     6→\n     7→## Summary\n     8→\n     9→The Planning Step is the first phase of the tddy-coder workflow. It accepts a user's goal description via stdin, invokes an LLM backend (Claude Code CLI) in plan mode, and produces a structured planning output: a named directory containing a `PRD.md` (Product Requirements Document) and a `TODO.md` (implementation task list).\n    10→\n    11→## Background\n    12→\n    13→tddy-coder is a strict, state-machine-driven TDD workflow orchestrator. It uses LLM-based coders (starting with Claude Code) as backends to drive development from planning through production. The planning step is the entry point of the workflow — before any code is written, the system must produce a clear requirements document and a structured execution plan.\n    14→\n    15→The tool treats the LLM as a subordinate: it instructs the LLM what to analyze, constrains its behavior via plan mode, and captures structured output. The LLM does not drive the workflow — the state machine does.\n    16→\n    17→## Requirements\n    18→\n    19→### CLI Interface\n    20→\n    21→1. Binary name: `tddy-coder`\n    22→2. Accepts `--goal plan` to trigger the planning step\n    23→3. Accepts `--output-dir <path>` to configure where planning output is written (defaults to current directory)\n    24→4. Accepts `--model <name>` (or `-m <name>`) to select the LLM model (e.g. `opus`, `sonnet`, `haiku`)\n    25→5. Reads the feature description from stdin (supports piped input and interactive prompt)\n    26→6. *Deferred*: `--list-models` to list available models (not needed for current scope)\n    27→\n    28→### Planning Workflow\n    29→\n    30→1. Read feature description from stdin\n    31→2. Invoke Claude Code CLI in plan mode to analyze the feature description\n    32→3. **Q&A phase**: Claude Code may ask clarifying questions; the user is expected to answer them. The system must support this interactive exchange (Claude asks → user answers → Claude continues analysis).\n    33→4. Generate a deterministic directory name based on the feature (date-prefixed, slugified)\n    34→5. Parse Claude Code's structured output into PRD and TODO artifacts\n    35→6. Write `PRD.md` and `TODO.md` to the output directory\n    36→7. Report success/failure with the output directory path\n    37→\n    38→### LLM Backend Abstraction\n    39→\n    40→1. The system defines a Rust trait (`CodingBackend` or similar) for LLM interactions\n    41→2. Claude Code CLI is the first concrete implementation\n    42→3. The trait must support: invoking the LLM, passing prompts, receiving structured output\n    43→4. The backend must support **model selection** (pass model name to the underlying CLI/API)\n    44→5. Tests use a mock implementation that allows test-controlled responses and behavior\n    45→\n    46→### Claude Code Integration\n    47→\n    48→1. Invokes `claude` CLI binary (from PATH)\n    49→2. Uses plan mode via `--permission-mode plan` (read-only analysis)\n    50→3. **Model selection**: Passes `--model <name>` to the `claude` binary when the user specifies one via `--model` / `-m`. Default model when unspecified (e.g. `opus` or backend default).\n    51→4. Supports **interactive Q&A**: Claude may ask clarifying questions during planning; the user provides answers. The invocation model must allow this exchange (e.g. multi-turn or interactive session).\n    52→5. Passes a system prompt instructing Claude to produce PRD and TODO content in a parseable format, or to output clarifying questions in `---QUESTIONS_START---` / `---QUESTIONS_END---` delimiters\n    53→\n    54→### Output Artifacts\n    55→\n    56→#### PRD.md\n    57→\n    58→- Feature summary and background\n    59→- Requirements (functional and non-functional)\n    60→- Acceptance criteria with checkboxes\n    61→- Impact analysis (if applicable)\n    62→\n    63→#### TODO.md\n    64→\n    65→- Implementation milestones broken into discrete tasks\n    66→- Tasks ordered by dependency\n    67→- Each task has a clear \"done\" definition\n    68→- Status tracking (pending/in_progress/completed)\n    69→\n    70→### State Machine\n    71→\n    72→1. The planning step is one state in the overall workflow state machine\n    73→2. It transitions from `Init` → `Planning` → `Planned` (or `Failed`)\n    74→3. The state machine enforces that planning must complete before development begins\n    75→4. State transitions are explicit and auditable\n    76→\n    77→## Acceptance Criteria\n    78→\n    79→- [ ] `tddy-coder --goal plan` reads from stdin and produces a named output directory\n    80→- [ ] Output directory contains well-formed `PRD.md` and `TODO.md`\n    81→- [ ] `--output-dir` flag controls output location\n    82→- [ ] `--model <name>` selects the LLM model; default used when omitted\n    83→- [ ] *Deferred*: `--list-models` lists available models\n    84→- [ ] Claude Code CLI is invoked in plan mode with appropriate arguments\n    85→- [ ] **Q&A support**: When Claude asks clarifying questions during planning, the user can provide answers and Claude continues analysis\n    86→- [ ] CodingBackend trait enables mock-based testing without real Claude Code CLI\n    87→- [ ] Tests use a fake/mock backend to verify the planning workflow end-to-end\n    88→- [ ] Error cases handled: empty input, Claude Code not found, malformed LLM output\n    89→- [ ] State machine enforces valid transitions\n    90→\n    91→## Future Considerations (Not In Scope)\n    92→\n    93→- Multi-turn refinement after initial plan (invoke → review → refine)\n    94→- Support for backends other than Claude Code\n    95→- File dependency analysis (Bazel-like)\n    96→- Test coverage and mutation testing integration\n    97→- Demo setup for user review\n    98→- Language-agnostic clean code analysis\n    99→"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01SDrSvr9LaXaNXSx4Fmjme9","session_id":"08af0f00-22d4-4762-903e-36c7a3c92f2b","uuid":"1ef703e2-6c7b-4fbf-a8be-6530b6bf1371"}

Real implementation that invokes `claude` CLI binary\n- `MockBackend` - Test implementation with controllable responses\n- `InvokeRequest` carries: prompt, system_prompt, permission_mode, model selection\n- `InvokeResponse` contains: output string, exit_code\n- `PermissionMode` enum: `Plan` (read-only) or `Default`\n\n**Output Parsing** (`packages/tddy-core/src/output/parser.rs`):\n- Parses delimited LLM output with markers:\n  - `---PRD_START---` / `---PRD_END---`\n  - `---TODO_START---` / `---TODO_END---`\n  - `---QUESTIONS_START---` / `---QUESTIONS_END---` (for clarification)\n- Returns `PlanningResponse` enum:\n  - `Questions { questions: Vec<String> }`\n  - `PlanningOutput { prd: String, todo: String }`\n\n**CLI Binary** (`packages/tddy-coder/src/main.rs`):\n- Accepts `--goal plan` (only \"plan\" supported currently)\n- Accepts `--output-dir <path>` (default: current directory)\n- Accepts `--model <name>` for model selection\n- Reads feature from stdin (interactive with inquire or piped)\n- Implements Q&A loop: if backend returns questions, prompts user for answers and re-invokes\n- Writes planning artifacts and reports success\n\n**Error Handling** (`packages/tddy-core/src/error.rs`):\n- `BackendError`: InvocationFailed, BinaryNotFound\n- `WorkflowError`: InvalidTransition, Backend, ParseError, WriteFailed, ClarificationNeeded\n- `ParseError`: MissingPrd, MissingTodo, Malformed\n\n**Planning Prompts** (`packages/tddy-core/src/workflow/planning.rs`):\n- System prompt instructs LLM to produce delimited PRD/TODO or questions\n- Build prompts: initial and follow-up (with user answers)\n\n---\n\n### 6. The planning step is the entry point of the workflow — before any code is written, the system must produce a clear requirements document and a structured execution plan.\n    14→\n    15→The tool treats the LLM as a subordinate: it instructs the LLM what to analyze, constrains its behavior via plan mode, and captures structured output. Accepts `--goal plan` to trigger the planning step\n    23→3. Accepts `--output-dir <path>` to configure where planning output is written (defaults to current directory)\n    24→4. Read feature description from stdin\n    31→2. Invoke Claude Code CLI in plan mode to analyze the feature description\n    32→3. **Q&A phase**: Claude Code may ask clarifying questions; the user is expected to answer them. The system must support this interactive exchange (Claude asks → user answers → Claude continues analysis).\n    33→4. Generate a deterministic directory name based on the feature (date-prefixed, slugified)\n    34→5. Parse Claude Code's structured output into PRD and TODO artifacts\n    35→6. Write `PRD.md` and `TODO.md` to the output directory\n    36→7. Report success/failure with the output directory path\n    37→\n    38→### LLM Backend Abstraction\n    39→\n    40→1. The system defines a Rust trait (`CodingBackend` or similar) for LLM interactions\n    41→2. Claude Code CLI is the first concrete implementation\n    42→3. The trait must support: invoking the LLM, passing prompts, receiving structured output\n    43→4. The backend must support **model selection** (pass model name to the underlying CLI/API)\n    44→5. Tests use a mock implementation that allows test-controlled responses and behavior\n    45→\n    46→### Claude Code Integration\n    47→\n    48→1. Invokes `claude` CLI binary (from PATH)\n    49→2. Uses plan mode via `--permission-mode plan` (read-only analysis)\n    50→3. **Model selection**: Passes `--model <name>` to the `claude` binary when the user specifies one via `--model` / `-m`. Default model when unspecified (e.g. `opus` or backend default).\n    51→4. Supports **interactive Q&A**: Claude may ask clarifying questions during planning; the user provides answers. The invocation model must allow this exchange (e.g. multi-turn or interactive session).\n    52→5. Passes a system prompt instructing Claude to produce PRD and TODO content in a parseable format, or to output clarifying questions in `---QUESTIONS_START---` / `---QUESTIONS_END---` delimiters\n    53→\n    54→### Output Artifacts\n    55→\n    56→#### PRD.md\n    57→\n    58→- Feature summary and background\n    59→- Requirements (functional and non-functional)\n    60→- Acceptance criteria with checkboxes\n    61→- Impact analysis (if applicable)\n    62→\n    63→#### TODO.md\n    64→\n    65→- Implementation milestones broken into discrete tasks\n    66→- Tasks ordered by dependency\n    67→- Each task has a clear \"done\" definition\n    68→- Status tracking (pending/in_progress/completed)\n    69→\n    70→### State Machine\n    71→\n    72→1. The planning step is one state in the overall workflow state machine\n    73→2. It transitions from `Init` → `Planning` → `Planned` (or `Failed`)\n    74→3. The state machine enforces that planning must complete before development begins\n    75→4. State transitions are explicit and auditable\n    76→\n    77→## Acceptance Criteria\n    78→\n    79→- [ ] `tddy-coder --goal plan` reads from stdin and produces a named output directory\n    80→- [ ] Output directory contains well-formed `PRD.md` and `TODO.md`\n    81→- [ ] `--output-dir` flag controls output location\n    82→- [ ] `--model <name>` selects the LLM model; default used when omitted\n    83→- [ ] *Deferred*: `--list-models` lists available models\n    84→- [ ] Claude Code CLI is invoked in plan mode with appropriate arguments\n    85→- [ ] **Q&A support**: When Claude asks clarifying questions during planning, the user can provide answers and Claude continues analysis\n    86→- [ ] CodingBackend trait enables mock-based testing without real Claude Code CLI\n    87→- [ ] Tests use a fake/mock backend to verify the planning workflow end-to-end\n    88→- [ ] Error cases handled: empty input, Claude Code not found, malformed LLM output\n    89→- [ ] State machine enforces valid transitions\n    90→\n    91→## Future Considerations (Not In Scope)\n    92→\n    93→- Multi-turn refinement after initial plan (invoke → review → refine)\n    94→- Support for backends other than Claude Code\n    95→- File dependency analysis (Bazel-like)\n    96→- Test coverage and mutation testing integration\n    97→- Demo setup for user review\n    98→- Language-agnostic clean code analysis\n    99→"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"08af0f00-22d4-4762-903e-36c7a3c92f2b","uuid":"4d519715-9c35-495e-9ca4-7535a86dc755","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/Users/mantasi/Code/tddy-coder/docs/ft/coder/planning-step.md","content":"# Planning Step — Feature Document\n\n**Product Area**: Coder\n**Status**: Draft\n**Updated**: 2026-03-06 (model listing/selection)\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Planning Step is the first phase of the tddy-coder workflow. It accepts a user's goal description via stdin, invokes an LLM backend (Claude Code CLI) in plan mode, and produces a structured planning output: a named directory containing a `PRD.md` (Product Requirements Document) and a `TODO.md` (implementation task list).\n\n## Background\n\ntddy-coder is a strict, state-machine-driven TDD workflow orchestrator. It uses LLM-based coders (starting with Claude Code) as backends to drive development from planning through production. The planning step is the entry point of the workflow — before any code is written, the system must produce a clear requirements document and a structured execution plan.\n\nThe tool treats the LLM as a subordinate: it instructs the LLM what to analyze, constrains its behavior via plan mode, and captures structured output. The LLM does not drive the workflow — the state machine does.\n\n## Requirements\n\n### CLI Interface\n\n1. Binary name: `tddy-coder`\n2. Accepts `--goal plan` to trigger the planning step\n3. Accepts `--output-dir <path>` to configure where planning output is written (defaults to current directory)\n4. Accepts `--model <name>` (or `-m <name>`) to select the LLM model (e.g. `opus`, `sonnet`, `haiku`)\n5. Reads the feature description from stdin (supports piped input and interactive prompt)\n6. *Deferred*: `--list-models` to list available models (not needed for current scope)\n\n### Planning Workflow\n\n1. Read feature description from stdin\n2. Invoke Claude Code CLI in plan mode to analyze the feature description\n3. **Q&A phase**: Claude Code may ask clarifying questions; the user is expected to answer them. The system must support this interactive exchange (Claude asks → user answers → Claude continues analysis).\n4. Generate a deterministic directory name based on the feature (date-prefixed, slugified)\n5. Parse Claude Code's structured output into PRD and TODO artifacts\n6. Write `PRD.md` and `TODO.md` to the output directory\n7. Report success/failure with the output directory path\n\n### LLM Backend Abstraction\n\n1. The system defines a Rust trait (`CodingBackend` or similar) for LLM interactions\n2. Claude Code CLI is the first concrete implementation\n3. The trait must support: invoking the LLM, passing prompts, receiving structured output\n4. The backend must support **model selection** (pass model name to the underlying CLI/API)\n5. Tests use a mock implementation that allows test-controlled responses and behavior\n\n### Claude Code Integration\n\n1. Invokes `claude` CLI binary (from PATH)\n2. Uses plan mode via `--permission-mode plan` (read-only analysis)\n3. **Model selection**: Passes `--model <name>` to the `claude` binary when the user specifies one via `--model` / `-m`. Default model when unspecified (e.g. `opus` or backend default).\n4. Supports **interactive Q&A**: Claude may ask clarifying questions during planning; the user provides answers. The invocation model must allow this exchange (e.g. multi-turn or interactive session).\n5. Passes a system prompt instructing Claude to produce PRD and TODO content in a parseable format, or to output clarifying questions in `---QUESTIONS_START---` / `---QUESTIONS_END---` delimiters\n\n### Output Artifacts\n\n#### PRD.md\n\n- Feature summary and background\n- Requirements (functional and non-functional)\n- Acceptance criteria with checkboxes\n- Impact analysis (if applicable)\n\n#### TODO.md\n\n- Implementation milestones broken into discrete tasks\n- Tasks ordered by dependency\n- Each task has a clear \"done\" definition\n- Status tracking (pending/in_progress/completed)\n\n### State Machine\n\n1. The planning step is one state in the overall workflow state machine\n2. It transitions from `Init` → `Planning` → `Planned` (or `Failed`)\n3. The state machine enforces that planning must complete before development begins\n4. State transitions are explicit and auditable\n\n## Acceptance Criteria\n\n- [ ] `tddy-coder --goal plan` reads from stdin and produces a named output directory\n- [ ] Output directory contains well-formed `PRD.md` and `TODO.md`\n- [ ] `--output-dir` flag controls output location\n- [ ] `--model <name>` selects the LLM model; default used when omitted\n- [ ] *Deferred*: `--list-models` lists available models\n- [ ] Claude Code CLI is invoked in plan mode with appropriate arguments\n- [ ] **Q&A support**: When Claude asks clarifying questions during planning, the user can provide answers and Claude continues analysis\n- [ ] CodingBackend trait enables mock-based testing without real Claude Code CLI\n- [ ] Tests use a fake/mock backend to verify the planning workflow end-to-end\n- [ ] Error cases handled: empty input, Claude Code not found, malformed LLM output\n- [ ] State machine enforces valid transitions\n\n## Future Considerations (Not In Scope)\n\n- Multi-turn refinement after initial plan (invoke → review → refine)\n- Support for backends other than Claude Code\n- File dependency analysis (Bazel-like)\n- Test coverage and mutation testing integration\n- Demo setup for user review\n- Language-agnostic clean code analysis\n","numLines":99,"startLine":1,"totalLines":99}}}

Parser for delimited PRD/TODO output from LLM.\n\nuse crate::error::ParseError;\n\nconst PRD_START: &str = \"---PRD_START---\";\nconst PRD_END: &str = \"---PRD_END---\";\nconst TODO_START: &str = \"---TODO_START---\";\nconst TODO_END: &str = \"---TODO_END---\";\nconst QUESTIONS_START: &str = \"---QUESTIONS_START---\";\nconst QUESTIONS_END: &str = \"---QUESTIONS_END---\";\n\n/// Result of parsing a planning response: either questions for clarification or PRD/TODO output.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub enum PlanningResponse {\n    /// Claude asked clarifying questions.\n    Questions { questions: Vec<String> },\n    /// Claude produced PRD and TODO.\n    PlanningOutput { prd: String, todo: String },\n}\n\n/// Parsed planning output containing PRD and TODO content.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct PlanningOutput {\n    pub prd: String,\n    pub todo: String,\n}\n\n/// Parse LLM planning response: either QUESTIONS or PRD/TODO. Returns Malformed if neither.\npub fn parse_planning_response(s: &str) -> Result<PlanningResponse, ParseError> {\n    if s.contains(QUESTIONS_START) && s.contains(QUESTIONS_END) {\n        let content = extract_section(s, QUESTIONS_START, QUESTIONS_END)\n            .ok_or_else(|| ParseError::Malformed(\"questions section incomplete\".into()))?;\n        let questions: Vec<String> = content\n            .lines()\n            .map(|l| l.trim())\n            .filter(|l| !l.is_empty())\n            .map(String::from)\n            .collect();\n        return Ok(PlanningResponse::Questions { questions });\n    }\n    if s.contains(PRD_START) && s.contains(TODO_START) {\n        let out = parse_planning_output(s)?;\n        return Ok(PlanningResponse::PlanningOutput {\n            prd: out.prd,\n            todo: out.todo,\n        });\n    }\n    Err(ParseError::Malformed(\"neither questions nor PRD/TODO found\".into()))\n}\n\n/// Parse LLM output that contains delimited PRD and TODO sections.\npub fn parse_planning_output(s: &str) -> Result<PlanningOutput, ParseError> {\n    let prd = extract_section(s, PRD_START, PRD_END)\n        .ok_or(ParseError::MissingPrd)?\n        .trim()\n        .to_string();\n\n    let todo = extract_section(s, TODO_START, TODO_END)\n        .ok_or(ParseError::MissingTodo)?\n        .trim()\n        .to_string();\n\n    Ok(PlanningOutput { prd, todo })\n}\n\nfn extract_section<'a>(s: &'a str, start: &str, end: &str) -> Option<&'a str> {\n    let start_idx = s.find(start)?;\n    let content_start = start_idx + start.len();\n    let rest = &s[content_start..];\n    let end_idx = rest.find(end)?;\n    Some(rest[..end_idx].trim())\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn extracts_prd_and_todo_from_delimited_output() {\n        let input = r#\"preface\n---PRD_START---\n# PRD\n\n## Summary\nFeature X\n---PRD_END---\nmiddle\n---TODO_START---\n- [ ] Task 1\n- [ ] Task 2\n---TODO_END---\ntrailing\"#;\n        let out = parse_planning_output(input).expect(\"should parse\");\n        assert!(out.prd.contains(\"Feature X\"));\n        assert!(out.todo.contains(\"Task 1\"));\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn errors_on_missing_prd() {\n        let input = \"---TODO_START---\\n- [ ] Task\\n---TODO_END---\";\n        let err = parse_planning_output(input).unwrap_err();\n        assert!(matches!(err, ParseError::MissingPrd));\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn errors_on_missing_todo() {\n        let input = \"---PRD_START---\\n# PRD\\n---PRD_END---\";\n        let err = parse_planning_output(input).unwrap_err();\n        assert!(matches!(err, ParseError::MissingTodo));\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn parse_planning_response_returns_questions_when_questions_delimiters_present() {\n        let input = r#\"preface\n---QUESTIONS_START---\nWhat is the target audience?\nWhat is the expected timeline?\n---QUESTIONS_END---\ntrailing\"#;\n        let resp = parse_planning_response(input).expect(\"should parse\");\n        match &resp {\n            PlanningResponse::Questions { questions } => {\n                assert_eq!(questions.len(), 2);\n                assert_eq!(questions[0], \"What is the target audience?\");\n                assert_eq!(questions[1], \"What is the expected timeline?\");\n            }\n            _ => panic!(\"expected Questions variant\"),\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn parse_planning_response_returns_planning_output_when_prd_todo_present() {\n        let input = r#\"preface\n---PRD_START---\n# PRD\n\n## Summary\nFeature X\n---PRD_END---\n---TODO_START---\n- [ ] Task 1\n---TODO_END---\ntrailing\"#;\n        let resp = X\"));\n                assert!(todo.contains(\"Task 1\"));\n            }\n            _ => panic!(\"expected PlanningOutput variant\"),\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn parse_planning_response_errors_on_malformed_when_neither_present() {\n        let input = \"Some random text without delimiters\";\n        let err = parse_planning_response(input).unwrap_err();\n
